Accident at Zhengtai Rubber Factory No. 1

Boiler Explosion Traced to Japanese Product

Chinese Boiler Remained Intact

Workers' Compensation to Be Decided at Shareholders' Meeting

Large Numbers of Charred Bodies Collected Separately Yesterday

Following the tragedy at the Zhengtai Rubber Factory No. 1 on Tangshan Road in Pudong, the factory began a three-day religious ceremony to pray for the deceased yesterday. The issue of compensation for the deceased workers will be decided at a shareholders' meeting after the investigation is completed. Reporters visited the factory at the end of Tangshan Road yesterday and investigated the cause of the accident. It has been learned that the factory has four steam boilers. The cause of the accident was a sudden explosion of the steam boiler located below the female workers' area. The female workers' area immediately collapsed in the explosion, and the flames spread rapidly, making it impossible for the female workers to escape. Fewer than 20% survived. According to the factory's war workers, the small steam boiler and the large steam boiler were made by the Xinmin Machinery Factory and remained intact even after the fire. This shows that the cause of the accident was entirely due to the inferior quality of Japanese goods sold to deceive people and proves the progress of China's machinery industry in recent years. The solidity of its structure and materials is indeed far superior to Japanese goods.

The North Gate Pushan Villa previously collected a large number of charred male and female corpses from the Zhengtai Rubber Factory on Tangshan Road in Pudong, temporarily placing them in coffins and transporting them to the villa for placement. For days, the families of the victims have been going to identify them. There are a total of 81 charred bodies. Three of them have been claimed by the families of the deceased. Yesterday, another eight bodies were identified by various families: (1) Ding Yuqin, female, from Boshan, Shandong; (2) Shen Minggui, male, from Qingyang; (3) Yu Renjin, male, also from Qingyang; (4) Ren Yongtang, male, from Jiangyin; (5) Zhu Simei, female, from Qingyang; (6) The mother of Zhang Lindi, female, local; (7) Zhang Damei, female, from Changzhou, 30 years old. The remaining male and female corpses are all charred, missing heads, hands, feet, or all four limbs, or only the abdomen remains, or intestines are flowing out of the abdomen. Various tragic scenes are unbearable to look at. Several of them have abdomens as large as buckets, resembling pregnant female corpses, which is extremely sad. They cannot be identified. Therefore, Wang Junsheng, the director of the villa, Yu Ruizhang, the accountant, and dozens of workers were assigned to collect the bodies. The coffins were purchased by the factory from the Jiangyin Guild Hall, costing 36 yuan each. The bottom of the coffin is lined with lime and grass. Each corpse is wrapped in silk and cotton, and covered with silk floss bedding on top and bottom. The bodies are then covered with sesame oil before being placed in the coffin. According to the staff of the villa, the corpses that cannot be identified will be transported by workers in cars to the Jiangyin Guild Hall cemetery near Dachan for burial.

The fire at the Zhengtai Rubber Factory on Tangshan Road injured and killed more than 200 workers, resulting in an unprecedented tragedy. The Party and government organs in this city are investigating the matter. The Central Civil Movement Committee also sent a telegram to the Municipal Party Committee, requesting to ascertain the truth. The General Labor Union in this city is paying particular attention to this matter. Yesterday, it specifically sent Executive Committee Member Gong Yuting to the factory to inquire about the fire and the workers' compensation matters. It is said that it will be proposed at today's regular meeting of the union for serious discussion and expression. In addition, rubber factory workers in District 1 also issued a declaration on the case yesterday.

Not Satisfied After Robbery

Abducted the Victim's Young Son

The Maid Also Disappeared at the Same Time

The Police Suspect It

Hu Henian, from Shaoxing, lives at No. 493 at the intersection of Huishan Road and Jingzhou Road in this city. His wife, Zhang, has a son and a daughter. His son, Guoan, is about to turn one year old. He hired a maid two months ago to do chores. Hu has been working as a securities runner at the World Bank on Fuzhou Road for many years. At around 1:40 AM yesterday, while Hu and his wife were fast asleep, four robbers suddenly came, one holding a pistol. They rushed upstairs and broke into Hu's bedroom. They first woke up Hu and his wife and demanded that they hand over their valuables. Hu had nothing to offer. The robbers then searched him and stole more than 20 yuan in cash and a gold watch. However, the robbers were not satisfied. They forced Hu to go with them. Hu told them that he was an ordinary person and that it would be useless to take him. Then, the robbers locked Hu and his wife in the back room and bolted it with wooden chopsticks. Then, they turned around and took Hu's young son, Guoan. After the robbers left, Hu and his wife shouted for help. The neighbors heard them and quickly got up to investigate and released Hu and his wife. They checked the room and found that the young son was missing. At the same time, the maid they had hired was also missing. They rushed to report to the Yulin Road police station. The police chief sent Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate and determined that the maid had disappeared suddenly during the robbery in the middle of the night and was highly suspicious. Moreover, the doors and windows were intact, with no signs of forced entry, indicating that there must have been an accomplice inside. Detectives were sent to the original employment agency to investigate the maid's background and apprehend the robbers.

Outside Wusongkou

Patrol Ships Seize Bandit Vessels

Land and Sea Police Surround from Four Sides

Guns and Sand Boats All Intercepted

The incident of pirates resisting arrest outside Wusongkou's Beigang sea area and being repelled by patrol ships has been reported in this newspaper. It is now known that at around 1:00 PM the day before yesterday, the captain of the 17th team of the 4th District of the Jiangsu Provincial Public Security Team, who is also the commander of the fleet, Xi Mianqin, and the captains of the "Cedian" gunboat, Lu Gongren, the "Jingdong" gunboat, Chen Zhentai, and the "Junhe" gunboat, Captain Zhang, as well as the "Jinghai" and "Pingyang" ships, were sailing through the East Sea. They saw a large sailboat ahead, carrying sixty or seventy people who appeared to be soldiers. The situation was very suspicious. The sand boat opened fire to resist arrest. Commander Gong, Captain Chen of the "Jingdong" ship, Captain Lu of the "Cedian" ship, and Captain Zhang of the "Junhe" ship jointly attacked from the left and right. The sailboat sped to the beach, where they landed and waded ashore. Commander Gong immediately telegraphed the Qidong County government. County Magistrate Fei immediately sent the nearby police captain Yin and the squadron leader Guan to lead their teams to pursue them overnight, surrounding them from four sides. They were finally intercepted and all firearms were confiscated. The seized sand boat and crew were handed over to the county government for detention and investigation by the fleet. Yesterday [blank] Stolen Goods Injured People Son of Famous Actress Xia Yuerun

Xia Bingjun's Home Robbed at Midnight

Bingjun and His Wife Were Both Seriously Injured and in Critical Condition

The Thieves Escaped Through the Window The Police Arrived After They Had Fled

At around 2:00 AM yesterday, a case of armed robbery and shooting occurred on Nanche Station Branch Road, which is under the jurisdiction of the Second District General Office of Nanshi. The victim was the eldest son of the famous actress Xia Yuerun. The details are recorded separately below.

Convoluted Residence Xia Bingjun, son of Xia, is from Anhui, 32 years old.

He currently resides at No. 161 Nanche Station Branch Road in Nanshi. He once worked at a can factory. Currently, he is unemployed at home. His wife, Chen Huizhen, is 29 years old. The residence at No. 161 is the ancestral property of Chen. The house is a three-story building located at the end of the alley, which is very convoluted. Xia and his wife live in the west wing room on the upper floor. The lower floor is rented to other households.

Sound of Knocking At around 2:40 AM yesterday morning,

Xia and his wife were fast asleep,

Suddenly hearing a knock on the door of the room, Xia

first heard it. Suspecting that it was a thief,

he coughed to scare them away. However, the sound of knocking grew louder and louder. Xia then woke up his wife, put on his clothes, left the bed, and approached stealthily.

Three Shots Fired When Xia arrived at the door and hurriedly pulled the bolt to look outside,

the person who came was holding a pistol. Seeing

Xia come out, he raised his arm and lunged at him.

The two wrestled together. Inside the room, miscellaneous objects were overturned. At the same time, Chen also joined in the resistance. As a result, the thief was unable to defeat them and pulled the trigger, firing three shots at Xia and his wife.

Husband and Wife Shot Xia's lower left ear

and Chen's abdomen were hit. They

both fell to the ground. Bleeding profusely, the perpetrator

took the opportunity to escape through the window. As he left, he also stole Chen's leather coat.

Xia and his wife groaned in pain for about half an hour before the police arrived.

Critical Condition When Xia and his wife were wrestling with the perpetrator,

Chen Weiqing, a tenant downstairs, initially

suspected that the couple upstairs were arguing. Until he heard

three gunshots, he realized something had happened.

He hurried to the Nanche Station Second District Police Station to report. The patrol chief Zhang Heshan led the police officers to the scene, the perpetrator had already disappeared. They telegraphed the general office and transported Xia and his wife to the hospital for treatment. The injuries were extremely critical.

Ordered to Arrest Immediately After the incident, Chief Jin of the district immediately

telegraphed the Supervision Office of the General Bureau. The Supervision Office

Statement from the Silver Ear Mushroom Industry Association

The Industry Does Not Have Japanese Goods

The Shanghai Silver Ear Mushroom Industry Association sent a letter to this newspaper stating: We respectfully note that yesterday (the 23rd), your newspaper published a news item titled "Japanese-Produced White Wood Ear Mushroom," which was translated from the Japanese Tokyo Jiji Shinpo. We were extremely shocked to read it. The white wood ear mushrooms sold by our industry in this city are all transported from Tongjiang, Taiping, and other counties in Sichuan, and Zunyi County in Guizhou, and sold in Shanghai. This has been the case for sixty years, and we have never heard of Japanese goods, let alone traded with foreign merchants. As this matter concerns the promotion of domestic goods, it is urgent to clarify the truth. Accordingly, we send this letter to request that you publish a statement in the letters column. Respectfully, the Shanghai Silver Ear Mushroom Industry Association, February 24.

Guo Weiyi Seduces and Rapes Lin Yayue

The Trial Was Closed to the Public

Only News Reporters Were Allowed to Attend

But the Details Were Not Recorded

Lin Yayue, from Chaozhou, hired three lawyers, Wu Kaisheng, Cai Xiaobai, and Ni Jiong, and filed a criminal self-complaint in the Second Special District Court, accusing Guo Weiyi, a fellow townsman and manager and chairman of Watson's Soda Company, residing at No. 23 Deming Lane, Baishi Road, French Concession, of seducing and raping her in the bathroom on the afternoon of June 17, 1923, and then abandoning her. She requested an investigation and sought civil damages. The court originally scheduled the trial for the afternoon before yesterday, but it was postponed due to lack of time. The trial was held at 2:00 PM yesterday. The original plaintiff, Lin Yayue, and her representative, lawyer Cai Xiaobai, reported to the court. The defendant, Guo Weiyi, and his defense lawyer, Lu Shaozong, also reported to the court to await the trial. At 2:30 PM, Judge Tai Huiping and clerk Tao Zongkan presided over the trial in the Fifth Court. Relatives and friends of both parties flocked to the benches to listen to the trial. After the judge took the bench and summoned the original plaintiff and defendant to inquire about their ages, hometowns, occupations, and addresses, he announced that the case was related to public morals and closed the trial to the public. Only news reporters were allowed to attend as a courtesy. The judge then inquired about the circumstances of the rape from the original plaintiff, Lin Yayue. After the original plaintiff finished speaking, she raised her left hand and said that the jade gold ring she was wearing was given to her by the defendant at that time. Due to the trial being closed to the public, the details were not recorded. The defendant denied the seduction and rape, saying that the original plaintiff was bought by his wife in his hometown as a maid. Later, her mother came to take her back to marry her off. She objected and did not want to go back. Later, because her mother often went to his home in the countryside to make a fuss, she had to be taken back. She was persuaded and sent back, and her mother signed a receipt. Then, the defense lawyer submitted a red paper document to the court. The judge asked the original plaintiff, who said that her mother did not sell her to the defendant, but she was raised in his home to take care of the children. The judge then advised the defendant to settle the matter. The defendant refused to agree. At this point, the judge declared that the interrogation was over and ordered the closing arguments. The original plaintiff's lawyer, Cai, stated that of the three lawyers hired by the original plaintiff, Wu and Ni were not present today, and the complaint still needed to be corrected to include abandonment. The defendant's document also had doubts and needed to be proven by her mother. He requested a postponement. The defendant's lawyer stood up to object. The judge said to the original plaintiff's lawyer that the point of abandonment could be filed in another case and that closing arguments could be held today without postponement. Then, the lawyers of both sides argued with each other. The court ordered the closing arguments to be terminated and scheduled the verdict for 2:00 PM on the 27th. Then, the court adjourned.

Li Zongtong

Discusses the First Batch of Antiquities Transported to Beijing Yesterday

According to the Central News Agency, Li Zongtong, Secretary-General of the Palace Museum, told a Central News Agency reporter yesterday that the 2,118 boxes of the first batch of antiquities transported south from the Palace Museum, the location of the storage had previously been decided by the Central Political Committee to be transported to Kaifeng and Luoyang for storage. Because it was difficult to find a suitable location in Kaifeng and Luoyang, the final decision was made to place them in the new building next to the Central Hospital in Nanjing. It has been decided to transport them to Beijing today (i.e., yesterday) via Pukou. As for the date of the south-to-north transportation of the first batch of antiquities, it will be determined after the vehicles transporting the first batch of antiquities return north. The quantity is difficult to predict, but it is known that various precious antiquities from the Antiquities Exhibition Hall of the Ministry of Internal Affairs will also be transported in the second batch. Although the number of antiquities in the Antiquities Exhibition Hall is 70% less than that of the Palace Museum, the famous bronze ware are all from the Song and Ming dynasties, and the portraits of emperors of past dynasties are even rarer.

League of Nations to Hear Further, Continued from Page 3 8

The foundation of the original covenant is about to be destroyed. Mr. Li concluded by saying, "This structure already shows signs of being unable to support itself. The hope of reducing world armaments has been jeopardized. The work of establishing international economic cooperation has been expanded. For these reasons, we must now vote to pass the Special Committee's report." The Venezuelan representative, Mr. Soumaye, then spoke, saying that whenever the League of Nations' mechanisms were faithfully and bravely put into use, effective results occurred. However, deviating from the covenant would hinder the possibility of a permanent solution. Now, there is bloody conflict in both the West and the East, as if the covenant did not exist. Observing the development of this conflict, it is felt that the covenant needs to be revised, and strengthening international jurisdiction and mediation under the supervision of the League of Nations is indeed necessary. However, any procedure that allows the state of violence that has existed since 1931 to persist and even increase should not be permitted. Delaying is not the best way to achieve peace; this kind of procedure is particularly dangerous." Finally,

The Lithuanian representative, Mr. Zaunius, spoke, urging the League of Nations Assembly to continue its efforts without slackening, and said that since mediation procedures have already been exhausted, appropriate and necessary plans should be adopted thereafter. In any case, once the report is passed, it must not become a mere formality. The result of the vote was unanimous passage. Chairman Hymans then

Announced the decision to vote and read out the articles of the covenant, explaining that "unanimous" means all members of the Administrative Council (excluding the disputing countries) plus a majority of the members of the League of Nations Assembly. Thereupon, a roll-call vote was taken, with forty-two countries in favor and only Japan against. Siam did not vote, and several countries were absent. After the vote, Hymans announced that the report had been passed unanimously.

Halting War Based on the Covenant and Reading out the Covenant

Article 15, Section 6, states that member states agree not to engage in war against a party that complies with the recommendations of the report. Article 12 of the covenant was also read out, stipulating that war may not be engaged in until three months after the report has been issued. Hymans also said that he hopes both sides can accept the efforts of mediation and that neither side will take irreversible actions that would prolong the dispute. The League of Nations should continuously seek solutions and continue the work entrusted to it by the covenant.

Matsuoka Yosuke Speaks for the Second Time

Then gave his second speech, expressing disappointment at the League of Nations' passage of this report, saying that Japan had participated in the work of drafting the League of Nations covenant and had worked with the world's major powers to achieve the highest purpose of uniting mankind. Japan was very proud of this. Japan's policy was fundamentally based on the idea of ensuring peace in the Far East and promoting peace throughout the world. He deeply lamented the current situation. Regarding the Sino-Japanese dispute, Japan has now reached the limit of its willingness to cooperate with the League of Nations, but Japan is still willing to participate in work that contributes to world peace.

The Japanese Delegation Leaves the Venue One After Another, Matsuoka Speaks

After finishing his speech, the members of the Japanese delegation left one after another. However, at that time, the meeting had already ended, and some people in the venue had already gotten up from their seats, so the impact of the Japanese delegation leaving the venue was not very noticeable. However, the Japanese delegation's posture was clearly understood. Anyone who knew the relationship was deeply impressed.

Matsuoka, Pale-Faced, Leads the Way Matsuoka's Face

Was pale, but he still had a resolute demeanor. Matsuoka led the way, followed closely by the other Japanese representatives. The seven or eight Japanese representatives attending the Disarmament Conference also followed behind. The crowd was crowded at the entrance of the venue. The Japanese delegation walked straight ahead through the crowd, not looking left or right. The only Japanese person left behind in the venue was Sugimura, who was a secretary of the League of Nations. Examining the intent of the Japanese representatives' words, it is still questionable whether Japan will sever relations with the League of Nations. However, it is generally expected that the Japanese government will take action to indicate this, presumably by directly notifying the Secretariat of its views. The General Assembly Adjourns and Will Continue in the Afternoon Hymans Announces

That the General Assembly will continue in the afternoon at 5:00 PM to discuss a certain point mentioned in the report (presumably regarding the establishment of a negotiating committee) and to accept a document. The full text of the report will be officially sent to the representatives of the United States and Russia stationed in Geneva, asking them to work with the League of Nations as quickly as possible to take consistent action. (Reuters dispatch, 24th)

The General Assembly Passes

Organizing an Advisory Committee

To Continue Handling the Sino-Japanese Conflict

Inviting the US and Russia to Participate in the Work

The General Assembly Will Not Adjourn and Can Be Convened at Any Time

(Geneva) The League of Nations General Assembly continued its meeting tonight. Our country's representative, Mr. Gu, spoke and gave a detailed account of the serious situation in Jehol. The General Assembly has passed a resolution to organize an advisory committee to assist the General Assembly in continuing to handle the Sino-Japanese conflict. The advisory committee will be composed of the members of the original Nineteen-Nation Special Committee and representatives from Canada and the Netherlands, and will invite the US and Russia to participate in the work. The General Assembly will remain in session and can be convened at any time the presiding officer deems necessary. (Central News Agency dispatch, 26th, 2:30 AM)

(Geneva) Chairman Hymans presented a draft resolution as follows: The League of Nations General Assembly, in accordance with Article 3, Section 3 of the Covenant, may deal with any event that hinders world peace at any meeting. Therefore, it cannot turn a blind eye to the development of the Sino-Japanese dispute. In accordance with Section 17 of Chapter 3 of the report passed by the League of Nations General Assembly in accordance with Article 15, Section 4 of the Covenant, member states of the League of Nations must not take unilateral action regarding the situation in Manchuria and must continue to act in concert with each other and with relevant non-member states. In order to facilitate the establishment of a situation in the Far East that is in accordance with the recommendations in the report, the Secretary-General is now instructed to send a copy of this report to the non-member states that signed the Kellogg-Briand Pact and the Nine-Power Treaty, informing them of the League of Nations General Assembly's hope that these countries will endorse the report's views and, if necessary, take consistent action and attitude with member states of the League of Nations. The League of Nations General Assembly decided to organize an advisory committee to monitor the situation and assist the League of Nations General Assembly in fulfilling its responsibilities under Article 3, Section 3 of the Covenant, with the aim of supporting member states in taking consistent action with each other and with non-members, so as to be in line with their attitude.

The Advisory Committee will be composed of the members of the Nineteen-Nation Special Committee and representatives from Canada and the Netherlands.

The Advisory Committee will invite the governments of the United States and Russia to participate in its work and will submit reports and recommendations when it deems appropriate, and will notify the governments of non-member states participating in the work of its reports. The League of Nations General Assembly will remain in session, and its chairman, after consultation with the Advisory Committee, may convene it when he deems appropriate. (Reuters dispatch, 24th)

(Geneva) Our country's delegation cabled the National Government tonight, saying to quickly withdraw the ambassador to Japan. (Central News Agency dispatch, 25th, 2:30 AM)

US Educators

Demand Recognition of the Soviet Union

Petition to Roosevelt

TASS dispatch from New York, 23rd: Eight hundred American professors, university presidents, and teachers, representing 268 universities and specialized schools in 45 states of the United States, recently submitted a petition to President-elect Roosevelt, requesting the United States to recognize the Soviet Union. The petition stated, "This is an indispensable step regarding world peace and the mutual economic interests of the two countries." Several of the signatories to this petition are well-known American scientists and economists, such as Professor Meek, Dean of the Experimental College of the University of Wisconsin, Dr. Dewey, Professor of Philosophy at Columbia University, Mr. Neilson, President of Smith College in Massachusetts, Dr. Commons, Professor of Political Economy at the University of Wisconsin, Professor Hudson, Professor of International Law at Harvard University, Professor Williams, Professor of Political Economy at the University of Pittsburgh, and Mr. Patterson, Professor of Economics at the University of Pennsylvania. Professor Niebuhr, one of the initiators of this petition, said, "Under the current emergency situation, the United States' failure to recognize the Soviet Union will pose a serious threat to world peace." He hopes that this petition will be sufficient to increase the tendency of Americans to care about and understand the Soviet Union, and hopes that the government and parliament will take appropriate steps in response to the submission of this petition.

Lord Lytton Expresses

Supplying Japanese Military Supplies is a Crime

Sufficient Assistance Should Be Provided to Countries Defending Themselves

And Cites the Story of Greece to Urge Japan to Wake Up

(London) Lord Lytton gave a speech in Norwich, England, today, mentioning the situation in the East, saying that stopping the export of military supplies would not pose any difficulty. He saw no reason why Britain should not supply China with military supplies. However, to prevent the military supplies to China from falling into the hands of Japan would not be easy. It is simply a crime for the government of a member state of the League of Nations to allow its citizens to continue selling military supplies to a country, enabling it to continue a war that is recognized by the world as unjust. Moreover, the League of Nations is bound by its own report and must provide all kinds of assistance to the other party. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

(London) Lord Lytton told a Daily Telegraph reporter today that the British government cannot impose an embargo on its own. It must first seek the consent of other members of the League of Nations before it can act. Britain initiated the conclusion of an international agreement, and no one can stop it, saying that it is inconceivable that any member state of the League of Nations can supply military supplies to either of the two countries in dispute while this dispute is under consideration by the League of Nations. If a ban is implemented, a clause should be added to the League of Nations Covenant to prohibit any member state from transporting military supplies to any other member state under consideration by the League of Nations. The Labour Party's demand not to sell military supplies to Japan is extremely legitimate. However, if other countries continue to transport military supplies for export, why should Britain be the only one to prohibit it? If the arms trade continues, why should Britain sacrifice its own interests to benefit other countries? Lord Lytton continued, saying that Japan has good reasons for the Manchurian case, but the actions it has taken are simply unreasonable and unwarranted. Lord Lytton also cited the position of Greece after the Greco-Turkish War, saying that at that time, the League of Nations' official, Mr. Venizelos, had gone astray, but before long, the Greeks overthrew their government and replaced it with a government with a new policy. Japan is now effectively ruled by warlords. All of Japan's friends now hope that the Japanese can take the same action. Now, as long as a mutually satisfactory solution is obtained, peace is still possible. The only solution is to completely remove the military equipment from the three eastern provinces, so that a capable police force commanded by foreign personnel can maintain order there. (Reuters dispatch, 24th)

(London) The Daily Express commented on the issue of banning military exports, saying, "If China or Japan entrusts a third country to purchase military supplies from England on their behalf, how will this be prevented? What is the definition of 'military supplies'? How will we deal with railway materials, oil, rubber, steel, chemicals, grain, textiles, leather boots, medicines, and other items necessary for war used to transport troops? If all are placed in the category of military supplies and banned, it is tantamount to implementing an economic boycott." (Reuters dispatch, 24th) Japanese Conspiracy to Burn Down

Soviet Aviation Station in Kamchatka

Instigator Arrested, Confession Confirmed

(Moscow) A report from Berlik mentioned that on January 19th, the Soviet civil aviation station in Ust-Bolsheryotsk, Kamchatka, suddenly caught fire. After investigation, it was found that the fire was deliberately set by Trofimov, a member of the local defense team assigned to guard the station, with the assistance of Prigov, another member of the defense team. Later, it was found that the two's arson was instigated by Serivalov, the shopkeeper of a local state-run farm. Serivalov was previously a monk. After examining the crimes of the three, it was found that they were also instigated by Jieze, a Japanese resident in Ust-Bolsheryotsk. Jieze was subsequently arrested. According to Jieze's confession, the confessions of Trofimov and Prigov were accurate. However, he was also ordered by another Japanese person to destroy the Soviet civil aviation station and other important state-owned buildings in Ust-Bolsheryotsk. (TASS dispatch, 23rd) British Parliament Inquiry

(London) During the House of Commons meeting today, a member of parliament asked Foreign Secretary Simon whether, in view of the seriousness of the situation in Jehol, he had ordered all British expatriates in the province to withdraw completely, and whether, as the Japanese army was about to invade North China, it was advisable to order all British expatriates in the counties of Hebei Province to withdraw and concentrate in Peiping or Tianjin. Important News from Fujian Province 11

Implementation of Literacy Education for the Public

Zheng Zhenwen, the Director of the Education Department of Fujian Province, regards the literacy movement as a crucial aspect of public education and pays exceptional attention to its implementation. He has thoroughly reviewed and finalized the General Outline of the Popular Literacy Education Plan, previously established by the Provincial Government. It has been submitted to the Provincial Affairs Council for approval and preparations have already begun. An excerpt of its contents is as follows:

The principle is to first designate Fuzhou City as a pilot area, and then divide the pilot area into appropriate locations as community experiment zones. All illiterate young people aged between twelve and twenty-five are to be compelled to attend school. The remaining districts will be promoted gradually. The study period is set at four months. Teaching staff will be comprised of government officials and education institution personnel to avoid any bias and ensure tangible results.

Organization: The Provincial Government will convene representatives from Party, government, military, academic, and social organizations to form a Popular Education Committee in the pilot area. They will work together to develop the undertaking, with the Chairman of the Provincial Government serving as Chairman and the Director of the Education Department as Vice-Chairman. A secretary will be appointed, along with various departments for general affairs, publicity, investigation, design, supervision, and inspection, ensuring that each duty has a specific responsible party and that matters are dealt with practically.

Publicity: A Popular Literacy Education Publicity Week will be held regularly to arouse the attention of literate citizens and encourage illiterate citizens to attend school. Efforts will be made to ensure that the methods are widespread and the impressions are profound.

Investigation: Following the Publicity Week, Saturday and Sunday will be selected as days for administrative agencies, schools, and social occupational organizations to assign personnel to form investigation teams to survey illiterate citizens within the area, aiming to ensure that no area is overlooked.

Design: There are detailed regulations regarding the formulation of literacy test standards, the division of experimental areas, the designation of public school locations, and the allocation of illiterate citizens to schools and teaching staff.

Funding: The total annual cost is 32,140 yuan, with monthly expenses of approximately 2,600 yuan. Two-thirds of the funds will be used for lighting and teaching materials, while one-third will be used for books, investigation certificates, publicity subsidies, and various administrative expenses.

Assessment: In addition to rewards for diligent teaching staff and penalties for those who are negligent, there will also be specific measures regarding the diligence and indolence of illiterate citizens during their schooling to ensure that tangible results are achieved within a reasonable period.

Municipal Education Bureau of This City 14

Attention to Female Education

Order to Municipal Public and Private Middle Schools

To Pay More Attention to the Discipline and Management of Female Students and Carefully Select Teachers

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to public and private secondary schools yesterday, stating: "The education of women in this city is just beginning to sprout and should be cultivated with great care to promote its development. However, recent reports indicate that middle schools for girls in this city have not paid sufficient attention to the hiring of teachers and the discipline and management of students. The pursuit of academic knowledge between teachers and students has been largely neglected, and the practice of etiquette has also been overlooked. Female education is almost criticized by society. The deeply ingrained bad habits should be corrected as soon as possible. Hereafter, middle schools that accept both male and female students must follow the provisions of this Bureau's Order No. 1155 to separate male and female school buildings and hire excellent female instructors to reside in the school. For schools that are exclusively for girls, the hiring of teachers and staff should prioritize the recruitment of female personnel as much as possible. If it is necessary to hire male teachers and staff, their academic and moral conduct must be carefully investigated before hiring them, so that the conduct of the employed personnel can serve as a role model, subtly influencing and transforming students. Students' character will be guided on the right track, and the academic atmosphere will change so that the development of female schools can be expected. All schools under your jurisdiction must abide by this order. The Director of this Bureau has high expectations." This order is issued.

Research Fellows of the Academia Sinica Arrive in Guilin

Fossils from a Million Years Ago Discovered

(Guilin Correspondence) Li Jie, Zhu Sen, Qiu Liwo, and others, research fellows of the Institute of Geology of the Academia Sinica, were dispatched to the Hunan-Guangxi region to study the structure of the Nanling Mountains and the origins of ore beds in various locations. Since their departure, they have entered Guangxi from Hunan and conducted detailed investigations along the way, gaining many insights into the study of mountain ranges and ore beds. They arrived in Guilin and, on the 11th, discovered a large number of vertebrate fossils (commonly known as dragon bones) and snail and clam fossils in a cave outside the North Gate. It is said that these fossils are remnants of organisms from a million years ago and are from the same period as the red clay deposits around the city. The red soil layer is widely distributed in southern China, and its formation period has been studied by geologists from home and abroad, but has not yet been resolved. Now that these fossils have been obtained, the age of the red soil can be estimated. This discovery is a great contribution to geology in our country and is truly good news for the scientific community.

Education Department and Schools Deduct Administrative Expenses and Teachers' Salaries

University, Middle School, and Elementary School Students Raise Funds to Be Completed Within Three Months

The 95th consultation and discussion meeting of the Yunnan Provincial Department of Education and the 30th regular meeting of the Third Committee of the Provincial Committee were held on the 6th as a joint meeting. Li Yongqing chaired the meeting, and Shao Run recorded the minutes. Matters discussed included: (1) Given the urgency of the national crisis, the educational circles of this province should initiate the raising of national salvation donations to provide resources for defense and aid national salvation. It was resolved that, in addition to making efforts in shame education and military training, the educational circles of the entire province should immediately practice frugality, appeal widely, and initiate the raising of national salvation donations with the goal of purchasing two fighter planes to contribute to the nation. The airplanes should be named "Yunnan Education" and "Yunnan Student" respectively. The purchase price should be based on raising more than one million old dollars. The methods for sharing the fundraising responsibilities are as follows: (1) The Department of Education, provincial schools, and educational institutions receiving provincial educational funding, as well as students studying abroad, will jointly raise more than 500,000 yuan. Starting in February, the Department of Education will deduct 20% of the department's funds each month. When schools and institutions apply for funds from the treasury, 20% will be deducted directly from the original amount. When collection agencies apply for red bonuses, 5% will be deducted directly. 2.5% will be deducted from the red bonuses of business agencies as donations, which will be saved in a special account by the treasury and remitted together with the principal and interest. However, temporary expenses with fixed amounts and the provisions for chaste women in the Jingjie Hall may not be deducted. For students studying abroad, 10% of their provincial fees and scholarships will be temporarily deducted from a certain month, and the Department will send letters to solicit the opinions of the students studying abroad before making a decision. The 20% deduction from schools and institutions includes personnel salaries and administrative expenses. After the deduction, personnel salaries will be reduced by 20%, and administrative expenses will also be tightly controlled by each school and institution, and expenditures will be made at 80% of the original amount. The internal allocation will be determined by the responsible personnel, but funds designated for specific purposes (such as library fees) can only be reduced by 20% according to the prescribed amount, and the remaining 80% will still be used for the prescribed purpose and reported, and cannot be misappropriated for other purposes. Military training expenses may not be reduced. In addition, all school and institutional personnel are also expected to donate freely according to their ability, and to solicit donations separately. Fundraising methods will be determined separately, and the fundraising will be reconsidered for suspension when more than 500,000 yuan has been raised. (2) Elementary school students throughout the province will be responsible for raising more than 100,000 yuan, with each student required to donate more than one yuan. This will be organized by the education bureaus of each county, city, and district and completed within three months, and delivered to the treasury of this department for verification and transfer. (3) University and middle school students throughout the province will be responsible for raising more than 100,000 yuan, with each student required to donate more than ten yuan. This will be organized by each school and completed within three months, and delivered to the treasury of this department for verification and group transfer. (4) Local education circles in counties, cities, and districts throughout the province will be responsible for raising 300,000 yuan, which will still be organized by each education bureau and completed and remitted within three months. However, if necessary, the full amount of elementary school education awards and bonuses will be used to cover expenses. (2) The program for the implementation of a full-time system in secondary schools throughout the province was resolved. Provincial schools in the provincial capital will implement the program step by step in accordance with the regulations. Provincial schools outside the province with three or more high school classes should treat the principal and part of the teachers according to high school standards. Those with less than three classes should treat the principal and all the teachers according to junior high school standards. Regardless of whether they are high or junior high schools, new full-time teachers who have just graduated from school and have not taught courses before should be paid from the lowest grade. For full-time teachers who have already been hired by various schools, a separate implementation sequence should be determined for those whose contracts have not yet expired this semester. As for part-time teachers in various schools, they should refer to the departmental regulations and be responsible for one-third of the extracurricular self-study guidance based on the number of teaching hours they are assigned. The detailed rules for handling the case were resolved, amended, and passed. (4) The municipal government designated various groups to organize the Former Anti-Japanese Association's Confiscated Goods Clearance Committee and sent a letter to inform the association to send personnel to participate. It was resolved to recommend Standing Director Huang Zaoxiong to participate as a representative. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Furthermore, when the staff member was reappointed as a teacher at Tangwan Elementary School, he was not clearly transferred by this bureau, which is considered an interruption, so the request cannot be approved. The total amount of funds raised is 2,207 yuan. At the meeting of donors, Pan Gongzhan, Xu Peixing, Zhao Lvqing, Chen Chupin, Yi Zhoujin, Xin and others were elected to form a fund management committee, responsible for supervising the use of the funds. Three deposit books were handed over to the family members of Mr. Bojun for safekeeping. In addition to issuing a letter of gratitude to the donors, an advertisement will be placed in the supplementary section of this newspaper to show credibility.

Summer Physical Education Tutoring Class

Admission Qualifications Have Been Determined

Based on the Principle of Recommendation

(Nanjing, 24th) The Ministry of Education has approved nine general rules for admission to the summer physical education tutoring class, the main points of which are: (1) Admission qualifications for students: incumbent physical education teachers in primary and secondary schools, staff members of public gymnasiums, teachers and staff members of martial arts halls, physical education administrative personnel in education administrative agencies, those who have considerable research and special interest in physical education and have obtained proof from the local education administrative agency. (2) Students are based on the principle of recommendation. Recommendation methods: each provincial education department at least four people, municipal education bureau or social affairs bureau two people, provincial and municipal martial arts halls two people, county and city education bureaus may recommend physical education administrative personnel from this bureau or two physical education teachers and staff members from their affiliated schools, halls and venues when necessary, and public and private schools may recommend one physical education teacher from this school when necessary. (3) Recommendation letters, registration lists, and half-length photos of students must be sent to the Association for review before May 1st. (4) Those who pass the review will be notified to come to Beijing from July 5th to 9th to complete various admission procedures.

Disappointing Women's Basketball Game

Two Rivers Defeated by Western United 23

Thirty-one to Twenty-three

Two Rivers Team's Performance Significantly Diminished

Lu Lihua Claims Unfair Refereeing

The Two Rivers Women's Basketball Team was defeated again by the Western Youth United Team last night with a score of twenty-three to thirty-one. Two Rivers was inferior from beginning to end. The audience's enthusiasm was not very high. This was the second performance for Two Rivers in preparation for going abroad.

Two Rivers Constantly Under Pressure. From the start, after Chen Rongming of Two Rivers scored one point from a free throw, Western Youth immediately surged ahead, leading three to one. Then they took the lead with seven to three. Although Two Rivers fought hard, they still trailed seven to nine at the end of the first quarter. However, Two Rivers ultimately failed to maintain their position. The momentum of Western Youth grew stronger and stronger. Two Rivers was completely trampled, eventually losing by a score of seven to nineteen. The first half ended with eleven to twenty-one. In the second half, Western Youth made slight adjustments but did not diminish their performance, adding another four points. As a result of Two Rivers' hard fight, they gradually improved, narrowing the gap to only seven points, nineteen to twenty-six. However, the final result was a defeat of twenty-three to thirty-one.

Jesson Truly Delightful. Western Youth assembled stars from both the Red and Blue teams. Their speed in passing the ball and the tightness of their defense were astonishing. The coordination, positioning, and beautiful passing of the three forwards were superior to Two Rivers. Especially Jesson, who was the most outstanding, scoring twenty-three points, which was truly commendable and made him a star. The failure of Two Rivers was obviously due to bad luck in the game, and also due to panicking because of the setbacks, missing many shots that should have been made, and making too many mistakes, which were exploited by the opponents. The three forwards were completely helpless under strict guarding, which was quite unexpected. The retreat of the guards was also broken by the opponent's triangular passing, creating a disadvantageous situation.

Two Rivers Claims Unfair Refereeing. According to Lu Lihua, the principal of Two Rivers, the failure of Two Rivers was the responsibility of the unfair refereeing. The Westerners should have been penalized but were not, which was clearly biased, making the heroes of Two Rivers unable to use their skills. There are still two more games, and they will negotiate with the Western Youth Sports Department to hire other referees. It is noted that the referee last night was Bennet of Western Youth, who is also a major defender of the Pirates team.
