Influence and Money 97

— Bō Píng

K, who had been unemployed for more than a year, got permission from his wife's uncle 丨丨 the deputy president of the S City Chamber of Commerce, thanks to his wife's influence. He actually entered the door of a magnificent, tall, and vast company. How rare this is! Among the unemployed friends, who doesn't congratulate him, who doesn't envy him, envy him for having such a reliable influence, and actually occupying a hard-won position among many petty bourgeois.

On the first day, K felt uneasy: obviously, it was the uneasiness that should be had when entering for the first time. The gazes of colleagues were raw and terrible, and their laughter was刺似的. Those wearing Western-style clothes were even more arrogant, but K had to bow his head, looking at the very wrinkled gray cloth gown on his body, what can be done! Enduring eight hours in silence, he was finally able to restore the comfort of that time.

But: the second day, the third day, still uneasy uneasy and uneasy. In addition to looking down on him, colleagues constantly satirized him, saying things like [to get a high position,] you should find someone with influence to help], and [to want money, you must first marry a wife,] now it's those who rely on their wives who are in the limelight]. Every time he heard these words, he felt pain in his heart. In the afternoon, his wife's uncle 丨 Deputy Chamber of Commerce President came, and several cunning and arrogant people rushed to say: [Mr. So-and-so, your relative is truly young and mature, also simple and silent, and will surely be a promising and capable person in the future.] The uncle wants to save face, and he knows that people are deliberately saying it to him, which is extremely embarrassing. He hurriedly turned around and left, and went to complain to K's wife. [As a company employee, you shouldn't still be like a beggar.] Businessmen rely on facades and socializing. What's the point of not opening your mouth all day long? It's not like a clay Buddha in a dilapidated temple. Running into the company's door, even the ancestors of my three generations have lost face, everyone knows that the relatives of the Deputy Chamber of Commerce President are like beggars.]

When K's wife red-facedly described the difficulties at home, the uncle frowned and ran away.

At half past four, when K returned home, he saw that his wife's eyes were extraordinarily red compared to the past. Ah! Money: Ah! Influence: K finally lost his job again on the fourth day.

Shop Clerk Communications

Child Bride 99

— Féng Yǒuzhāng

Dear Editor:

I am a child under the age of seventeen, and according to the norm, I am still in the golden age of schooling; however, due to the constraints of my environment, I cannot help but drop out of school and go into business. I think that these three years of apprenticeship are really the key to my whole life: if I learn well, I will benefit for a lifetime, and if I don't learn well, I will have no prospects for the rest of my life. Thinking like this, how hard should I work! But my vexing marriage problem prevents me from seizing this key to my whole life and building the foundation of my future without any slack.

When I was five years old, I was engaged to a little girl surnamed Rong through the words of a matchmaker; she has been a child bride in my family since she was a child. She is the daughter of a farmer in the countryside and has never been to school; so she knows nothing about [emotion] [elegance]... I do not have a strong objection to this. The most distressing thing is that her upper limbs are not flexible enough, which makes things very difficult. In addition, she is nearsighted, so she needs someone to serve her.

Therefore, I have various questions; now I will write them down one by one; please reply to me in detail: (1) Ordinary people, when marrying a wife, naturally hope that she can manage the household affairs. Can my fiancée be competent? (2) When she first came to my house, she was very lively, but she became like this after a illness; so should we bear considerable responsibility? (3) Although she is so deformed, my mother loves her very much; if I propose to cancel the engagement, can my future be realized smoothly? (To be continued)

Respectfully,

Feng Youzhang

Editor's note: The system of child brides is very common in Chinese society. It has two drawbacks; first, because the marriage contract was made when they were young, when the boy and girl grow up and become adults, they cannot cooperate with each other, and when they want to cancel the contract, disputes will inevitably arise. Second, because most mothers-in-law are ignorant of reason and regard child brides as slaves, not only do they not give them the opportunity to be educated, but they mostly add unreasonable abuse, so [child bride temper] has become a special idiom. But we believe that if they can be raised by their side like adopted daughters, cherish them, teach them everywhere, and give them as many educational opportunities as possible. After both parties are adults, obtain their consent, and then make an engagement and marriage, then there are advantages. First, because the boy and girl have lived together since they were young, they can naturally understand each other; if they do not express any objection when the engagement is held after adulthood, they must be in agreement. Second, because before marriage, they have long been a part of the family, so they can adapt to everything. Third, because the girl's education is fully provided by the husband's family, the levels of both parties can be equivalent. The above is our general opinion on the [child bride] system.

Now let's discuss Mr. Feng's question. First, Mr. Feng's mother is able to be different from ordinary mothers-in-law and is very fond of her child bride; so I dare to say that her not having gone to school is due to environmental reasons, not because of any discrimination. You see, she has to teach her beloved Mr. Feng to drop out of school and go into business! Fortunately, Mr. Feng's mind is clear in this environment, otherwise he will inevitably seek [emotion] [elegance], but will end up in boredom! Second, ordinary people, when marrying a wife, naturally hope that she can manage the household affairs, but this is not a very difficult task after all, and if she is not disabled, she can barely be competent. According to the letter, Mr. Feng's mother is still very fond of her daughter-in-law, so she is definitely not disabled, at most she is a little deformed. Third, some human diseases can of course be cured, but there are also those that cannot be cured at all. Mr. Feng's fiancée has been raised at home since she was a child, so she must be treated when she gets sick. Mr. Feng's mother, having loved her so much, must have assumed considerable responsibility and treated her; so it can be said that she has fulfilled her responsibilities and does not bear any responsibility. However, we should also pity and support such a poor person. Fourth, because we cannot be very sure about the situation of Mr. Feng's fiancée, we cannot answer his question decisively. Our answer is that if she has not reached the point of being disabled, it may be wise to agree for the sake of pitying her. If she is unfortunately really a disabled person, then she can only cancel the engagement; under these conditions, not only your mother will not insist, but even her parents cannot object.

Novel 100

Coal Hill (Continued) 101

— Ed Falkowski Translated by Sui

Two

Saturday brought a bustling and messy scene to the main street. Cafes, clothing stores, goldsmiths, and five-and-dime stores all flaunted their brilliance, illuminating the continuous stream of people along the roadside. Saturday also made everyone feel happy. People leisurely strolled along the road with their wives or innocent female workers.

Customers crowded in and out of store A and store B. The cash registers of the five-and-dime stores were constantly spinning. Hardworking saleswomen ran urgently behind the counters, and friendly customers constantly came and went. Howling cars jammed the crossroads of the main street's red and green traffic lights. The police sucked on cigarettes and spat out the ashes.

[Rest] is the hope of injecting new life into the blood, and the painful joints can barely forget their pain. The tired brains are excited by the bright street lights and attracted by the movie theaters showing interesting films. Burly managers sat behind their desks, planning as they looked out the window. They spent the whole day dreaming of making commercial profits. [Success] is something that everyone can 丨 or should 丨 achieve. The city's poor people live in dark alleys. Some bungalows are Italian taverns, and the cellars are inhabited by Lithuanians and Poles, who are filled with endless grief due to the pain of life. Saturday nights are also lively for them. Accordion music flowed from these houses.

Women wearing wool scarves sneaked out of the taverns with bottles for their husbands. [Why don't you go out, Peter? You've been home for a week. It's Saturday night, you should have fun.]

[Your friends can't see you anywhere, they will forget everything about you.] [Who are my friends, Mary? Everyone is drinking with companions, but after drinking, everyone disperses. In this city, no one can be called my true friend. To tell you the truth, I am very sad about life in the mine, even to the point where everyone, you feel disgusted, and good times are spent in the mine.]
